2:22:1344:0:14:72:345:700:12:Times:12:Times:F:Is the U.S. Losing Its Preeminence in Higher Education?
2:23:1399:14:14:72:153:686:12:Times:12:Times:F:James D. Adams
2:24:1413:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:F:NBER Working Paper No. 15233
2:25:1441:14:14:72:134:658:12:Times:12:Times:F:August 2009
2:26:1452:14:28:72:197:644:12:Times:12:Times:F:JEL No. I23,J31,L31,O31
2:27:1475:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:28:1483:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:F:The expansion of U.S. universities after World War II gained from the arrival of immigrant scientists
2:29:1584:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:and graduate students, the broadening of access to universities, and the development of military research
2:30:1689:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:and high technology industry. Since the 1980s, however, growth of scientific research in Europe and
2:31:1788:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:East Asia has exceeded that of the U.S., suggesting convergence in world science and engineering
2:32:1884:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:and a falling U.S. share. But the slowdown of U.S. publication rates in the late 1990s is a different
2:33:1985:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:matter, in that the rise of science elsewhere does not imply a U.S. slowdown in any obvious sense.
2:34:2083:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:F:Using a panel of U.S. universities, fields and years, evidence is found of a slowdown in the growth
2:35:2182:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:of resources.  In turn, this has caused a deceleration in the growth of research output in public universities
2:36:2292:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:and university-fields falling into the middle 40 percent and bottom 40 percent of their disciplines.
2:37:2392:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:These developments can be traced to slower growth in tuition and state appropriations in public universities
2:38:2500:14:42:72:459:448:12:Times:12:Times:F:compared to revenue growth, including from endowment, in private universities.
2:39:2578:42:14:72:153:406:12:Times:12:Times:F:James D. Adams
2:40:2592:14:14:72:198:392:12:Times:12:Times:F:Department of Economics
2:41:2615:14:14:72:226:378:12:Times:12:Times:F:Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute
2:42:2647:14:14:72:217:364:12:Times:12:Times:F:3406 Russell Sage Laboratory
2:43:2675:14:14:72:183:350:12:Times:12:Times:F:Troy, NY  12180-3590
2:44:2695:14:14:72:124:336:12:Times:12:Times:F:and NBER
2:45:2703:14:0:72:151:322:12:Times:12:Times:F:adamsj@rpi.edu
3:46:2717:0:24:108:235:705:257:Times:257:Times:C:I. Introduction 
3:47:2732:24:28:90:524:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:For more than half a century U.S. universities have led the world in research and graduate 
3:48:2823:28:27:71:532:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:education, building on firm foundations laid down in the 19th century, and rising to new heights 
3:49:2920:27:28:72:532:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:during the 20th century.  But in recent years doubts have begun to arise concerning the future of 
3:50:3018:28:28:72:536:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:U.S. higher education, considered as a producer of graduate and professional students as well as 
3:51:3115:28:27:72:528:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:scientific discoveries.  The two are complementary: faculty that are not at the research frontier 
3:52:3213:27:28:72:532:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:are less likely to produce top PhDs and MDs, and conversely, faculty who lack top students are 
3:53:3308:28:27:72:536:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:less likely to do cutting-edge research.  It follows that this paper’s emphasis on research extends 
3:54:3408:27:28:72:500:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to advanced students1.  Furthermore, a strong research enterprise improves the quality of 
3:55:3498:28:28:72:517:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:undergraduate education in the long run and contributes to the ability to undertake advanced 
3:56:3591:28:27:72:413:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:training.  As far as higher education is concerned, none of this is new.  
3:57:3665:27:28:90:537:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The U.S. is losing share in scientific research, and perhaps in papers accepted in top journals 
3:58:3761:28:27:71:506:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Hicks, 2007), in part because the number of countries that devote significant resources to 
3:59:3853:27:28:72:496:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:scientific research has increased.  This implies intensified competition for scientific and 
3:60:3945:28:27:72:531:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:engineering talent and also greater competitiveness of foreign high technology firms (Freeman, 
3:61:4040:27:28:72:515:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:2006).  But in addition to growth overseas, a slowdown has taken place within the U.S. The 
3:62:4131:28:28:72:528:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:growth rate of financial resources of U.S. public universities has declined and this has reduced 
3:63:4228:28:27:72:542:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the growth rate in their publications2.  This development is important, because public universities 
3:64:4328:27:28:72:272:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:account for a large share of U.S. science. 
3:65:4371:28:27:90:517:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:It may come as a surprise to hear that U.S. universities could be in danger of losing their 
3:66:4463:27:28:72:531:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:preeminence, since top U.S. private and public universities invariably rank near the pinnacle of 
3:67:4560:28:20:72:503:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:world institutions (Shanghai Jiao Tong University, various years).  But university growth 
3:68:4650:20:8:108:254:109:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
3:69:4710:8:16:72:542:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:1 In confirmation of this point, the National Research Council rankings of graduate programs reveal a strong positive 
3:70:4828:16:7:71:503:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:correlation between research and the quality of graduate programs.  See National Research Council (1995). 
3:71:4934:7:0:72:310:78:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:2 See Ehrenberg (2006) and Adams and Clemmons (2009). 
4:72:4992:0:27:72:531:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:overseas implies that this dominance may not last forever.  Moreover, public universities in the 
4:73:5089:27:28:72:246:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:U.S. have struggled in recent years. 
4:74:5126:28:27:90:530:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:To understand how top private universities in the U.S. have reached unparalleled heights at 
4:75:5218:27:28:72:505:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the same time that top public universities have fallen behind, it is necessary to explain the 
4:76:5312:28:28:72:520:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:organization of U.S. higher education.  It is a mixed public-private system.  Top U.S. private 
4:77:5407:28:27:72:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities rely on federal grants, endowment, gifts, and tuition to hire the best faculty, select 
4:78:5507:27:28:72:522:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the best students, and sustain their competitive advantage.  In this they are not constrained by 
4:79:5604:28:27:72:539:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:state interests.  The situation is otherwise with U.S. public universities, whose charter, beginning 
4:80:5705:27:28:72:543:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with the Morrill Act of 1862, enjoins them to support state industries by providing affordable and 
4:81:5804:28:28:72:542:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:practical higher education.  If state budgets contract, or if competition for state funds strengthens, 
4:82:5907:28:27:72:529:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:then funding diminishes and the competitive advantage of U.S. public universities declines.  A 
4:83:6002:27:28:72:512:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:pillar of public support for higher education, its accountability to state interests, erodes and 
4:84:6099:28:27:72:555:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:becomes a constraint on university growth.  In recent years this appears to have taken place.              
4:85:6206:27:28:90:503:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The paper’s focal point is a panel of universities and fields observed over time.  Main 
4:86:6294:28:27:72:516:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:findings from an analysis of these data are as follows.  Starting with growth facts, I find that 
4:87:6391:27:28:72:512:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:research output grows at about the same rate in the late 20th century in private schools as in 
4:88:6486:28:28:72:533:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:public, until the 1990s, when public university growth slows down.  This is despite the fact that 
4:89:6584:28:27:72:543:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:stocks of Research and Development (R&D), which are mostly federally funded, rise appreciably 
4:90:6678:27:28:71:542:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:faster in public universities.  A slowdown in papers and in papers per dollar of R&D is evident in 
4:91:6777:28:27:72:531:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the late 1990s, again in public universities.  Given the challenges of measuring R&D, I provide 
4:92:6873:27:28:72:526:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:faculty counts as a supplementary measure.  It turns out that faculty grow at a slower rate than 
4:93:6970:28:28:72:533:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:papers so research productivity indeed rises.  Once again, though, it rises more slowly in public 
4:94:7068:28:0:72:540:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities, especially during the late 1990s.  In addition, the evidence reveals that current funds 
5:95:7174:0:27:72:528:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rise more rapidly in private universities, suggesting that in public universities, faster growth of 
5:96:7274:27:28:71:530:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(mostly federal) R&D stocks is cancelled by slower growth in tuition and state appropriations.  
5:97:7370:28:27:71:523:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Hence, faster growth of current funds in private schools contributes to faster growth of wages 
5:98:7465:27:28:71:321:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and research output in these universities.                  
5:99:7525:28:28:89:512:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:  Continuing with regression findings, I show that public and private universities obtain 
5:100:7615:28:27:71:500:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:similar percentage increases in scientific papers and citation-weighted papers from equal 
5:101:7705:27:28:72:509:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(percentage) increases in R&D, graduate students, and current funds, so that differences in 
5:102:7797:28:27:72:516:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:growth of research output between the two sets of institutions are the result of differences in 
5:103:7893:27:28:72:528:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:growth of resources.  Here private universities have recently held the advantage.  Departments 
5:104:7988:28:28:72:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:ranked in the top 20 percent of their disciplines obtain a larger increase in papers for the same 
5:105:8086:28:27:72:518:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increase in R&D and students than departments of lower rank.  Graduate students contribute 
5:106:8177:27:28:72:514:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:more to papers in top 20 percent departments than elsewhere, suggesting the high degree of 
5:107:8268:28:27:72:488:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:complementarity of faculty and graduate students at the top of the quality distribution. 
5:108:8357:27:28:90:535:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Compensation in private universities rises faster than it does in public universities by almost 
5:109:8453:28:27:72:542:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:one percent per year.  Compared to public universities, where the wage structure is relatively flat, 
5:110:8554:27:28:72:545:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compensation in private schools is higher at all ranks and rises more markedly for full professors.  
5:111:8655:28:28:72:535:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:This suggests incentives for researchers, especially senior researchers, to migrate from public to 
5:112:8754:28:27:72:528:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:private universities.  Combined with slower growth in current funds in public universities, this 
5:113:8851:27:28:72:511:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:helps to produce slower growth in their research output than in that of private universities.  
5:114:8946:28:27:90:487:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The rest of the paper proceeds as follows.  Sections II and III provide an historical 
5:115:9032:27:28:72:489:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:perspective on U.S. universities.  Section II recounts the expansion of research in U.S. 
5:116:9121:28:28:72:524:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities before, during, and after the Second World War.  This is the period in which U.S. 
5:117:9216:28:0:72:537:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities progress relative to the rest of the world.  Section III considers the U.S. contribution 
6:118:9322:0:27:72:519:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to world scientific output since the 1980s.  The share of the U.S. declines sharply during this 
6:119:9418:27:28:72:478:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:period.  While this is inevitable in the face of postwar recovery and world economic 
6:120:9503:28:27:72:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:development, the section also points to a slowdown in research output during the 1990s in the 
6:121:9597:27:28:72:518:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:U.S., due largely to a deceleration in the growth rate of resources in U.S. public universities. 
6:122:9694:28:28:90:517:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Section IV introduces panel data covering 110 top U.S. universities and 12 main science 
6:123:9782:28:27:72:508:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:fields during 1981-1999.  Section V presents growth facts concerning university research.  
6:124:9873:27:28:72:506:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Section VI begins with regressions in which research output is the dependent variable and 
6:125:9963:28:27:72:537:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:concludes with wage regressions.  Section VII discusses the evidence and draws conclusions for 
6:126:10058:27:32:72:245:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the future of U.S. higher education. 
6:127:10095:32:27:108:400:456:257:Times:144:Times:C:II. U.S. Universities Since World War II 
6:128:10134:27:24:108:242:429:257:Times:144:Times:C:A. Pre-War Setting 
6:129:10152:24:28:108:477:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: Prior to World War II and quite unlike the present day, federal Research and 
6:130:10229:28:27:72:536:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Development (R&D) was located inside the U.S. military (Mowery and Rosenberg, 1989, pages 
6:131:10319:27:28:72:536:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:92 ff.).   Agricultural research is the exception.  It was conducted in land-grant colleges founded 
6:132:10419:28:27:72:515:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:by the Morrill Act of 1862 and the Land-Grant Act of 1890, extending the 1862 Act to state 
6:133:10510:27:28:72:531:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:agricultural and mechanical colleges for blacks.  In addition, the Hatch Act of 1887 established 
6:134:10607:28:28:72:504:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:experiment stations close to the land-grant colleges.  Huffman and Evenson (1993, Ch. 1) 
6:135:10696:28:27:72:330:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:provide a moving summary of these developments3.   
6:136:10747:27:28:108:526:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The first statistical evidence on university R&D in the U.S. derives from balance sheet 
6:137:10835:28:75:72:511:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:data in 1935-1936. The data are contained in Research—A National Resource, Volume I 
6:138:10918:75:8:108:254:109:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
6:139:10978:8:16:72:516:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:3 The democratic and equal-opportunity conditions set by the early U.S. patent system (Khan, 2005) may have 
6:140:11086:16:11:71:538:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:complemented the later establishment of universities focused on the agricultural and mechanical arts—the very type 
6:141:11201:11:0:71:192:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:envisaged by the Morrill Act. 
7:142:11235:0:27:72:520:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(National Resources Committee, 1938, Section 6)4.  A survey of 60 universities yielded total 
7:143:11328:27:28:72:539:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:research expenditures of 50 million $.  Of this amount, 16 million was earmarked for experiment 
7:144:11424:28:27:72:528:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:stations, much of this funded by the Department of Agriculture5.  Of the remaining 34 million, 
7:145:11519:27:28:72:527:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:17 derived from endowment, 8 from foundations, 4 from gifts, 2 from contract research, and 2 
7:146:11612:28:28:72:542:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:from state government.  Therefore, the federal government’s main role in university research was 
7:147:11709:28:27:72:206:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:its support for agriculture.   
7:148:11740:27:28:108:529:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: Bush (1945, P. 86) contains estimates of research expenditure by sector from the 1930s 
7:149:11827:28:27:72:539:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:through World War II.  The data are limited to natural science6.  Using as a basis the figure of 50 
7:150:11927:27:28:72:532:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:million $ reported in National Resources Committee (1938), this yields 25 million $ for natural 
7:151:12023:28:28:72:534:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:science research in 1936.  Using survey data on research faculty, this figure is then extrapolated 
7:152:12122:28:27:71:536:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:backward to 1930 and forward to 1942 to arrive at natural science R&D for universities.  This is 
7:153:12219:27:28:71:351:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the relatively crude university series shown in Figure 17.   
7:154:12280:28:27:108:542:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: The above summarizes the prewar setting.  Events surrounding World War II led to a vast 
7:155:12368:27:28:72:512:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:expansion of university R&D.  First, before the war, immigration of scientists from Europe 
7:156:12459:28:27:72:532:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:significantly increased the science and engineering work force. Second, during the war, a sharp 
7:157:12555:27:28:72:530:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rise in defense research increased the demand for scientists and engineers, which the Cold War 
7:158:12650:28:28:72:540:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:institutionalized8.  Third, after the war, the GI Bill helped finance college education for returning 
7:159:12752:28:27:72:540:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:soldiers, which subsequently produced a spike in enrollments and increased post-war demand for 
7:160:12847:27:23:72:298:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:faculty.  I discuss each of these factors in turn. 
7:161:12898:23:7:108:254:189:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
7:162:12958:7:16:72:540:182:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:4 Individual evidence on university R&D exists before 1935-1936.  The University of Chicago conducted an internal 
7:163:13072:16:12:72:527:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:survey of research costs in 1929-1930 and the University of California undertook a similar survey in 1928-1929.  
7:164:13185:12:7:72:434:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:But these data lack the comparative breadth of the National Resources Committee survey. 
7:165:13273:7:16:72:529:147:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:5 In 1940 federal R&D expenditures were 74 million $, of which 29 million $ or 39%, consisted of Department of 
7:166:13384:16:11:71:536:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Agriculture R&D (Mowery and Rosenberg, 1998, p. 27).  Clearly, agricultural research assumed a much larger role 
7:167:13496:11:7:71:321:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:in the federal government and universities than it does today.  
7:168:13560:7:12:72:514:113:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:6 In these early data, natural science includes biological, mathematical and physical science, plus engineering. 
7:169:13673:12:16:72:528:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:7 Industrial R&D statistics are obtained by multiplying industrial researchers by R&D per worker of 4,000 $.  See 
7:170:13787:16:7:71:488:85:100:Times:100:g_d0_f3:F:Research—A National Resource, Volume II (National Resources Planning Board, 1941, Section IV). 
7:171:13882:7:0:72:531:78:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:8 By an increase in demand I mean throughout a shift to the right of the demand curve for scientists and engineers. 
8:172:14002:0:24:99:486:705:257:Times:144:g_d0_f3:C:B. The Intellectual Migration from Europe, 1933-1944      
8:173:14059:24:28:108:518:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: The supply of highly skilled scientists to the United States increased due to the flight 
8:174:14148:28:27:72:532:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:from Hitler’s Europe, but by how much, and in what proportion?  The main statistical source is 
8:175:14243:27:28:72:486:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Davie (1947), who directed data collection for the Committee for the Study of Recent 
8:176:14328:28:28:72:534:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Immigration from Europe9.  Using the criterion of “refugee, arrival from Europe as place of last 
8:177:14425:28:27:72:485:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:residence”, statistics of immigration and naturalization yielded 22,842 refugees in the 
8:178:14513:27:28:72:525:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:professions during 1933-1944.  The refugees were assigned to detailed occupations: 507 were 
8:179:14605:28:27:72:530:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:chemists, 2,471 engineers, 3,415 professors and teachers, and 1,907 were “scientists or literary 
8:180:14702:27:28:72:527:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:persons,” yielding a total of 8,300 refugees in science, engineering and related professions.  In 
8:181:14800:28:28:71:529:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1938 the National Resources Committee, using American Men of Science, 6th Edition (1938), 
8:182:14890:28:27:71:521:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:estimated that 28,000 U.S. men and women were researchers in the natural sciences, and that 
8:183:14982:27:28:71:531:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:22,000 more were in the humanities and social sciences (National Resources Committee, 1938, 
8:184:15074:28:27:71:517:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:p. 171) for a total of 50,000 across all sectors of the economy10.  Thus, while the intellectual 
8:185:15171:27:28:71:518:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:migration from Europe during the 1930s was small by modern standards, it was large for the 
8:186:15262:28:27:71:514:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:time.  Put another way, if half of the roughly 8,000 refugees in science and engineering and 
8:187:15355:27:28:71:509:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:related fields were engaged in research—not excessive, given their occupations—then this 
8:188:15444:28:28:71:531:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:constitutes an increase of 4,000 persons on a base of 50,000, or 8%. And since they specialized 
8:189:15540:28:27:71:534:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in natural science and engineering, then the increase could be almost 4,000 on a base of 28,000, 
8:190:15637:27:68:72:121:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:or 14%11. 
8:191:15647:68:8:108:254:144:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
8:192:15707:8:16:72:508:136:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:9 Fermi (1971) recounts individual biographies of this wave of immigrants by detailed occupation, including 
8:193:15815:16:12:71:512:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:scientists and engineers by their separate specialties. Her time period, 1930-1941, is earlier than that of Davie 
8:194:15929:12:7:71:231:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:(1947), whose perspective I adopt here. 
8:195:15969:7:11:72:512:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:10 The Committee judged that of the existing stock of 50,000 researchers, 5,000 or 10% were in the first rank. 
8:196:16080:11:16:72:535:90:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:11 Following the usage of Bush (1945) and Davie (1947), in this section natural science refers to biology, medicine, 
8:197:16197:16:0:72:400:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:mathematics and statistics, and engineering, in addition to chemistry and physics. 
9:198:16284:0:27:108:545:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: There is reason to think that even this understates growth at the highest levels of research.  
9:199:16379:27:28:72:514:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Table 1 illustrates12.  Twelve refugees had won a Nobel Prize by 1947, the most prestigious 
9:200:16471:28:27:72:537:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:international award13.  Using a sample collected by Davie (1947) of 707 refugees who served on 
9:201:16566:27:28:72:532:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:university faculties in Europe, 203 persons were accounted distinguished in their disciplines, of 
9:202:16664:28:28:72:501:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:which 181 were in natural science.  To assess the meaning of this, turn to Table 2, which 
9:203:16754:28:27:72:538:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compiles U.S.-resident Nobel Prize winners by decade.  The number of foreign-born is shown in 
9:204:16848:27:28:72:539:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:parentheses for each subject area, except for the sum across areas, where the foreign-born appear 
9:205:16946:28:27:72:513:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:as column two14.  Noting that 23 prizes had been won by U.S. residents by 1940, with none 
9:206:17036:27:28:72:504:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:foreign-born except for one award, I conclude that the intellectual migration from Europe 
9:207:17126:28:28:72:313:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increased resident Nobel Prize winners by 50%15. 
9:208:17175:28:27:108:530:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: Table 2 also shows that major improvements in U.S. universities were underway by the 
9:209:17260:27:28:72:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1930s.  Across areas, the number of native-born prizes rises from one to 17 per decade during 
9:210:17354:28:27:71:529:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1901-1940.  Excluding economics prizes—since these did not exist until 1969—the total of 17 
9:211:17446:27:32:72:455:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:prizes for the 1930s is half the native-born total, per decade, during 1971-2007. 
9:212:17528:32:23:99:451:318:257:Times:144:Times:C:C. Increase in Federal R&D During World War II

9:214:17666:28:28:72:509:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increase in military R&D during and after the war produced a sustained rise in demand for

10:231:19135:27:32:71:461:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:R&D expenditures were on defense, the Atomic Energy Commission, or NASA. 
10:232:19208:32:23:99:392:511:257:Times:144:g_d0_f3:C:D. Postwar Demand for Higher Education  
10:233:19245:23:28:90:539:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Mobilization produced a wartime decline in male college enrollment and degrees.  But under 
10:234:19336:28:28:72:533:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the GI Bill this decline was succeeded by a large spike around 1950.  Figure 3 shows B.A.-B.S.

10:236:19522:27:28:72:515:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:decline from a peak of 100 thousand in 1940 to a trough of 50 thousand in 1946, and finally 
10:237:19614:28:27:72:527:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:spike to 350 thousand in 1950.  By comparison, the decline and recovery of degrees earned by 
10:238:19707:27:28:72:520:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:women are slight.  As the stock of excess demand for education diminished during the 1950s 
10:239:19798:28:27:72:465:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:baccalaureate degrees fell and did not regain their 1950 peak until the mid 1960s.

10:243:20156:27:34:72:261:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:long-run prospects for advanced skills.

12:284:23670:27:28:72:533:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:The charts show an accelerating decline in the U.S. share of citations, though nowhere is this as 
12:285:23768:28:27:72:517:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:great as the decline for papers.  The EU-15 gain share; and the share of East Asia, while it is 
12:286:23864:27:28:72:527:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:small, grows the fastest. At the end of the period, because of gains in Europe, 75% of citations 
12:287:23961:28:28:72:426:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:are still received by America and Europe compared with 70% at the start. 
12:288:24034:28:27:90:533:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Figure 10 depicts the U.S. share in the top 1%, top 5%, and top 10% most cited papers from 
12:289:24125:27:28:72:541:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1992-200526.   The share erodes at every level, and though it is hard to see the percentage decline 
12:290:24225:28:27:72:536:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is less for top 1% papers than top 5% papers.  The top 1% share declines from 65% of the world 
12:291:24320:27:28:72:518:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:total in 1992 to 55% in 2005.  This is a decline of 15 percentage points (10/65).  The top 5% 
12:292:24414:28:28:71:539:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:share declines from 38% to 30%, a decline of 21 percentage points.  So erosion in share is less at 
12:293:24513:28:27:71:435:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:higher levels of citation impact, though some may see this as cold comfort. 
12:294:24589:27:28:89:512:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:But what does all this mean?  Share data tell us little about welfare. Output adjusted for 
12:295:24680:28:27:71:523:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:quality, and output relative to input, are what matter for growth and technical efficiency of an 
12:296:24777:27:28:72:532:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:industry, and universities are no exception to this rule.  All we can say is that the growth rate of 
12:297:24878:28:27:72:524:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:U.S. scientific publications has fallen and that growth is slow relative to other regions, but we 
12:298:24976:27:28:72:349:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have not addressed the factors that drive this slowdown.   
12:299:25035:28:28:90:530:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Foreign competition for science and engineering students is unlikely to be responsible27.  If 
12:300:25129:28:38:71:536:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that were the reason, then the skill of foreign science and engineering graduate students entering 
12:301:25228:38:8:108:254:201:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
12:302:25288:8:11:72:414:193:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:25 The data source is Appendix Table 61, Chapter 5, National Science Board (2008).  
12:303:25372:11:12:72:414:182:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:26 The data source is Appendix Table 63, Chapter 5, National Science Board (2008).  
12:304:25456:12:16:72:534:170:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:27 In the long run, arguments concerning the diffusion of science and R&D vary in their implications for welfare of 
12:305:25572:16:11:72:520:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:advanced countries like the U.S.  If technology converges in science and in industrial research then the share of 
12:306:25686:11:12:72:536:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:innovative products produced in advanced countries will decline. Standard models build on the theory of trade with 
12:307:25801:12:11:72:524:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:differentiated products (Helpman and Krugman, 1986).   North-South models of innovation, imitation, and trade 
12:308:25911:11:12:72:539:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:based on this approach (Krugman, 1979; Grossman and Helpman, 1991) assume that all innovation occurs in North, 
12:309:26022:12:11:72:540:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:while South merely imitates.   But if advanced human resources arise in South as well, then innovation is distributed 
12:310:26140:11:12:72:518:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:across both North and South, as Freeman (2006) points out.  In that case the profits from new products are also 
12:311:26252:12:11:72:535:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:distributed across both regions and North can lose some industries with supra-normal profits.  Applying this line of 
12:312:26369:11:0:72:521:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:reasoning to universities as an industry suggests that the U.S. could lose the lead in some sciences which in turn 
13:313:26489:0:27:72:493:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:U.S. universities would have undergone serious decline in recent years.  But this seems 
13:314:26577:27:28:72:509:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:implausible given the attractiveness of U.S. education and employment.  Alternatively, the 
13:315:26668:28:27:72:500:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:slowdown could represent crowding out of U.S. authors in top journals (Hicks, 2007), or 
13:316:26756:27:28:72:529:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:diversion to commercial activities (Toole and Czarnitski, 2007), or earmarking to less efficient 
13:317:26853:28:28:71:313:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:institutions (De Figueiredo and Silverman, 2006). 
13:318:26903:28:27:89:538:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The recent slowdown could derive from other domestic causes and this is the approach that I 
13:319:26995:27:28:71:519:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:am about to pursue.  I show in Section V that growth of scientific publication in U.S. private 
13:320:27090:28:27:71:508:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities did not slow down much in the 1990s compared with the 1980s.  In contrast, a 
13:321:27180:27:28:71:497:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:pronounced deceleration did occur in public universities.  In explaining the difference, a 
13:322:27271:28:28:72:537:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:deceleration in resource growth during the 1990s seems to be the most likely explanation for the 
13:323:27368:28:31:72:475:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:slowdown in public universities.  I explore this hypothesis in Sections V and VI.      
13:324:27455:31:28:108:360:401:257:Times:144:g_d0_f3:C:IV. Panel Data on U.S. Universities 
13:325:27489:28:23:135:289:373:257:Times:144:g_d0_f3:C:A. Data Construction   
13:326:27510:23:28:90:515:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:With the goal of explaining the slowdown in U.S. academic research, I turn to empirical 
13:327:27598:28:27:72:519:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:work using a panel of 110 top U.S. universities.   I begin by describing the data.  In their raw 
13:328:27695:27:28:72:536:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:form they consist of 2.4 million scientific papers, published during 1981-1999, that have at least 
13:329:27794:28:28:72:530:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:one author from a set of leading U.S. universities.  These universities account for more than 80 
13:330:27891:28:38:72:338:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:Times:B:percent of U.S. academic research during this period28. 
13:331:27946:38:12:108:541:201:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                                                                                                                                                 
13:332:28123:12:12:72:519:189:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:might contribute to less effective industrial research in the U.S.  But countervailing forces also apply if product 
13:333:28239:12:11:72:525:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:varieties grow with the world economy. First, knowledge flows to industries in advanced countries will increase, 
13:334:28352:11:12:72:520:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:including universities, so that scientific discoveries and inventions of new products could increase.  Second, the 
13:335:28467:12:11:72:529:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:larger world economy that results from South’s entry into advanced nation status would create markets for North, 
13:336:28580:11:7:72:543:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:including in scientific research.  So it is not clear whether North gains or loses as a result of South’s development.      
13:337:28704:7:16:72:533:136:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:28 According to National Science Board (2002), Appendix Table 5-4, in 1999 the top 100 U.S. universities account 
13:338:28817:16:12:72:542:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:for $22.10 billion of R&D out of $27.49 billion of R&D for all U.S. universities.  This equals 80.4 percent.  National 
13:339:28936:12:11:72:520:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Science Board (2008), Appendix Table 5-11 indicates that in 2006 the top 100 account for $38.09 billion out of 
13:340:29047:11:12:72:531:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:$47.76 billion for all U.S. universities.  This equals 79.8 percent.  Since the sample consists of the top 110 and not 
13:341:29166:12:11:72:515:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:the top 100, its share in R&D expenditures exceeds 80 percent.  Publication data reflect R&D spending, so the 
13:342:29276:11:0:72:250:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:publication share also exceeds 80 percent.    
14:343:29327:0:27:108:536:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Papers consist of articles, reviews, notes, and proceedings.   The data source is Thomson-
14:344:29417:27:28:72:534:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Reuters Scientific29.   Papers follow the field that Thomson assigns to the journal in which they  
14:345:29516:28:27:72:509:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:appear30.  Field in this case is one of 88 subfields.  To link the data to the National Science 
14:346:29612:27:28:71:550:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Foundation’s (NSF) CASPAR database, I assign each of the 88 to one of NSF’s 12 main fields31.    
14:347:29709:28:28:108:487:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The data record publication year, journal field, institutional affiliation, address 
14:348:29793:28:27:72:506:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:information on city, state, and country, and author names as well as number of authors32.   
14:349:29885:27:28:71:542:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Address information is used to identify university affiliations of those who collaborate on a paper 
14:350:29985:28:27:71:532:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and to compute fractional papers.  By fractional, I mean that if a paper is written by researchers 
14:351:30084:27:28:71:539:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in two universities, then each university is assigned half the paper. If three collaborate, then each 
14:352:30186:28:28:71:519:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:receives a third, and so on33.  I add up fractional papers by university, field, and year to form 
14:353:30284:28:27:72:503:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:“effective” papers produced in a university-field.  By treating the data in this way I avoid 
14:354:30377:27:28:72:538:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:multiple counting of papers of U.S. universities taken as a whole.  Likewise I compute (forward) 
14:355:30474:28:27:71:529:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:citations received by a paper in its first five years including year of publication, and I calculate 
14:356:30575:27:28:71:531:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:fractional five-year citations in the same manner as for papers, but excluding citations from the 
14:357:30673:28:64:71:511:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:same institution.  I accumulate fractional citations by university, field, and year to form an  
14:358:30769:64:7:108:254:258:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
14:359:30829:7:16:72:502:251:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:29 The journal set consists of approximately 5500 journals that were active in 1999 as well as 1600 inactive 
14:360:30938:16:7:72:349:235:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:(renamed or out of print) journals that were cited by active journals.  
14:361:31010:7:16:72:534:228:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:30 This assignment is reasonable for specialized journals because of the breadth of fields that I use.  But the method 
14:362:31129:16:12:72:539:212:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:produces serious errors for the one percent of journals (about 70) that fall into Thomson-Reuters’s Multidisciplinary 
14:363:31247:12:11:72:523:200:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:category.  Thomson treats this category as part of biology because biology accounts for the largest number of its 
14:364:31361:11:12:72:526:189:100:g_d0_f3:100:Times:F:papers.  Multidisciplinary journals include Nature, Science, Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences 
14:365:31470:12:11:72:518:177:100:Times:100:g_d0_f3:F:USA, and Philosophical Transactions of the Royal Society.  Wholesale assignment to biology here is clearly 
14:366:31577:11:12:72:490:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:wrong.  But to correct the problem would require article (not journal) assignments to fields.  Also, some 
14:367:31683:12:11:72:539:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Multidisciplinary journals are primarily focused on biology.  Therefore, the problem applies to less than one percent 
14:368:31801:11:7:72:135:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:of the journals. 
14:369:31818:7:16:72:526:136:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:31 The twelve fields are: agriculture, astronomy, biology, chemistry, computer science, earth sciences, economics 
14:370:31932:16:7:72:439:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:and business, engineering, mathematics and statistics, medicine, physics, and psychology.   
14:371:32024:7:12:72:532:113:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:32 There is no limit on the number of authors.  The maximum number in the sample is 210 while the mean is 2.36.  
14:372:32137:12:16:72:540:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:33 The cumulative distribution of universities listed on papers is: 1 university, 79.6%; 2 universities or less, 96.8%; 3 
14:373:32259:16:11:72:541:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:universities or less, 98.3%; and 4 universities or less, 99.5%.  It follows that the fractions assigned are almost always 
14:374:32381:11:0:72:141:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:1, ½, 1/3, or ¼.   
15:375:32405:0:27:72:428:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:estimate of “effective” citation-weighted papers in a university-field34.      
15:376:32484:27:28:108:536:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:These steps yield research “output” in a university, field and year. Following along these 
15:377:32575:28:27:72:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:lines I form a panel of universities, fields and years.  The panel combines papers and citations 
15:378:32672:27:28:72:535:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with university-field level (R&D), university-field PhD students and post-doctoral students, and 
15:379:32769:28:28:72:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics of doctoral programs; as well as financial characteristics of parent universities.  
15:380:32869:28:27:72:528:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:The measure used for R&D is a calculated depreciated stock based on past R&D expenditures. 
15:381:32960:27:28:72:522:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:The NSF-CASPAR database of universities, a compendium of NSF surveys, is the source for 
15:382:33048:28:27:72:522:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:university R&D and for graduate and post-graduate students.  The HEGIS (Higher Education 
15:383:33137:27:28:72:522:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:General Information Surveys) surveys of the U.S. Department of Education provide financial 
15:384:33228:28:28:72:515:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:data at the university level on tuition revenues, state appropriations (for public universities), 
15:385:33326:28:27:72:531:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:endowments, auxiliary revenues from fees, and total revenues.  The National Research Council 
15:386:33419:27:28:72:540:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(NRC) 1993 Survey of Doctoral Programs (NRC, 1995) includes rankings of PhD programs, and 
15:387:33509:28:27:72:345:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:I use these to stratify departments by relative standing35. 
15:388:33569:27:28:108:541:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:In the basic panel of universities I consider only leading university-fields (“departments”) 
15:389:33662:28:27:72:514:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:from the top 110. Their number depends on size of field: I include the top 25 universities in 
15:390:33756:27:28:71:540:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:astronomy, the top 50 in agriculture, chemistry, computer science, economics and business, earth 
15:391:33853:28:28:71:499:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sciences, mathematics and statistics, physics, and psychology, and the top 75 in biology, 
15:392:33943:28:27:71:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:medicine, and engineering.  Summing across fields, and accounting for the fact that 48 formal 
15:393:34037:27:28:71:511:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:schools of agriculture exist, the panel consists of 648 top university-fields.   My purpose in 
15:394:34132:28:64:71:520:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:breaking out few individual schools in small fields and more in large fields is to avoid empty 
15:395:34227:64:7:108:254:120:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
15:396:34287:7:16:72:536:113:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:34 It is tempting to think of university-fields as departments, but this is misleading.  The same field can be practiced 
15:397:34408:16:7:72:469:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:by more than one department and (rarely) multiple fields can be practiced within one department.   
15:398:34507:7:16:72:534:90:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:35 NRC ranks are not available for agriculture and medicine.  For these fields I sort universities by their 1998 R&D 
15:399:34624:16:0:72:445:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:and assign a rank of 1 to the university with the largest R&D and so on in descending order.  
16:400:34723:0:27:72:537:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cells for universities where fields are small or non-existent36.   The result is a panel that contains 
16:401:34826:27:28:72:526:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:papers and citation-weighted papers for 648 university-fields in 12 main sciences during 1981-
16:402:34920:28:27:72:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1999.  This implies a total of 12,312 observations before exclusions due to missing values.  In 
16:403:35016:27:28:72:513:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:some cases I stratify the data into top 20 percent, middle 40 percent, and bottom 40 percent 
16:404:35109:28:28:71:540:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:university-fields.  A field that contains 50 university-fields has 10 in the top 20 percent, 20 in the 
16:405:35212:28:27:71:514:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:middle percent, and 20 in the bottom 40 percent, and so on.  The university-field dimension 
16:406:35304:27:28:71:510:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:allows for greater variability of R&D stock, graduate students, and other variables within a 
16:407:35397:28:27:71:522:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:university.  It increases the robustness of the findings when university dummies are included. 
16:408:35492:27:28:71:537:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:The price of this detail is that lagged faculty counts must be replaced by lagged R&D stocks and 
16:409:35589:28:28:71:521:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:a moving average of graduate students. These are the primary indicators of resources that are 
16:410:35683:28:31:71:302:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:available at the university, field and year level.  
16:411:35735:31:24:135:300:401:257:Times:257:Times:C:B. Descriptive Statistics 
16:412:35760:24:27:108:508:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 3 contains descriptive statistics for major variables. The table reports means, 
16:413:35846:27:28:72:544:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:standard deviations, minima, and maxima.  Groups consist of all, private, and public universities.  
16:414:35946:28:27:72:390:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:The last two are the groups used in the rest of the empirical work. 
16:415:36014:27:28:108:515:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:I begin with research output.  Mean (fractional) papers in all universities are 177 per 
16:416:36102:28:28:72:490:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:university-field and year. They are slightly larger in private schools.  The data indicate 
16:417:36193:28:27:72:532:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:considerable variation, especially among private schools.  The field with the most papers is in a 
16:418:36291:27:28:72:507:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:private university. The mean of five-year (fractional) citations received (citation-weighted 
16:419:36384:28:27:72:517:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:papers) is 520 per university, field and year.  This is 33% higher in private schools and 17% 
16:420:36478:27:60:72:439:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:lower in public schools.  Again the maximum occurs in a private university. 
16:421:36554:60:7:108:254:97:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
16:422:36614:7:16:72:518:90:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:36 The size of the remainder of the top 110 equals an average university-field in the individual top 25, 50, or 75 
16:423:36729:16:0:72:539:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:schools.  This reflects the positive skew of academic R&D.  For more on this point see Adams and Griliches (1998). 
17:424:36849:0:27:108:539:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:For comparison I report faculty counts.  Since these exist only at the university level they 
17:425:36942:27:28:71:522:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:indicate total research labor37.  The average school employs slightly more than 1,200 faculty; 
17:426:37037:28:27:72:512:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:private schools employ 800; and public schools employ 1,500.  A smaller faculty in private 
17:427:37128:27:28:72:527:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:schools produces the same papers per university-field, but appreciably more citation-weighted 
17:428:37222:28:28:72:531:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:papers, than do faculty in public schools.   Note that I compare total faculty in universities with 
17:429:37322:28:27:72:494:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:papers and citations at the university-field level. But this comparison is also valid at the 
17:430:37415:27:28:72:308:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:university level (Adams and Clemmons, 2009).   
17:431:37462:28:27:107:546:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Research & Development (R&D) stock signifies lagged resources that enter into research.  
17:432:37551:27:28:72:530:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:It is the depreciated sum of total R&D from federal and other sources in a university-field over 
17:433:37648:28:28:72:523:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the previous 8 years38.  The depreciation rate is 15%; underlying R&D flows are expressed in 
17:434:37741:28:27:72:523:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:millions of ’92 dollars using the BEA university R&D deflator (Robbins and Moylan, 2007).  
17:435:37832:27:34:72:293:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:R&D stock in fieldi, universityj, at timet is

17:450:38939:16:7:72:357:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:therefore the maximum length of stock that is available given the data.

18:453:39172:0:27:72:508:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in science and engineering (Ehrenberg, Rizzo, and Jakubson, 2007).  Not surprisingly, and 
18:454:39262:27:28:72:520:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:despite smaller enrollments, private schools have larger tuition revenues and larger (non-tax) 
18:455:39357:28:28:72:501:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:endowments.  State appropriations capture the “tax endowment” of public universities.  I 
18:456:39446:28:30:71:396:625:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:construct the following measure of current revenue in universityj:
