18:458:39573:25:28:72:533:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:In (2) Public is a dummy indicator equal to one in public universities and zero otherwise so that 
18:459:39671:28:27:72:535:542:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in private universities revenue is tuition, since Public equals zero. But in public universities it is 
18:460:39774:27:28:72:522:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tuition plus state appropriations on the assumption that appropriations substitute for tuition in 
18:461:39872:28:28:72:524:487:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:public universities. I lack a history of revenue, but I lag (2) by one year in the research output 
18:462:39971:28:27:72:534:459:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:equations to approximate lagged resources.  I treat endowment separately from revenue, since it 
18:463:40067:27:28:72:538:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is a stock, and since it may be earmarked for different uses. Note that I use the endowment stock 
18:464:40165:28:27:72:367:404:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:because endowment income is poorly measured in HEGIS.    
18:465:40222:27:28:108:509:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The moving average of the stock of graduate students over the previous three years 
18:466:40305:28:32:72:267:349:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:captures numbers of research assistants: 
18:467:40346:32:0:72:333:317:144:g_d0_f3:48:g_d0_f3:B:(3)  ττ−=∑=tijij, t ,
18:468:40366:0:13:268:271:325:48:g_d0_f3:48:g_d0_f3:?:3
18:469:40367:13:20:275:349:312:48:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:?:1Students*0.333Students Graduate 
18:470:40398:20:28:72:493:292:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Table 3 shows that public universities employ more graduate students.  But numbers of 
18:471:40484:28:28:72:511:264:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:undergraduates are also larger, requiring more of the graduate students to serve as teaching 
18:472:40577:28:27:72:536:236:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:assistants.  Besides this, large public university programs in engineering include masters as well 
18:473:40676:27:28:72:525:209:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:as PhD students.  For these reasons, (3) is likely to be a noisy indicator of research assistance, 
18:474:40775:28:27:71:272:181:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and yet it is the best measure that I have.  
18:475:40820:27:28:107:512:154:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:I use the ratio of auxiliary/total revenues (from HEGIS) to indicate financial duress. 
18:476:40907:28:0:71:507:126:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Auxiliary revenues are fee-for-service charges for residence halls, food services, athletics, 
19:477:41006:0:27:72:539:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:student unions, stores, and movie theaters40.  I divide auxiliary by total revenues to abstract from 
19:478:41107:27:28:72:497:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:size of university.  The mean of this ratio is 0.10,  although it ranges from zero to 0.30.   
19:479:41201:28:27:107:537:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:To motivate the use of auxiliary/total revenues, suppose that tuition is price-controlled in 
19:480:41294:27:28:71:541:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:a public university.  This could occur in states that guarantee tuition to families of students, since 
19:481:41397:28:28:71:523:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the states must then cover tuition if the price cap were to be lifted (Rizzo, 2006).  If fees were 
19:482:41496:28:27:71:510:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increased in small amounts, then they might substitute for tuition in this setting.  Likewise, 
19:483:41591:27:28:71:533:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:private universities with small endowments and gifts could use fees to finance their operations.  
19:484:41689:28:27:71:436:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Fees in this interpretation resemble hidden prices for university attendance. 
19:485:41767:27:28:107:522:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 4 reports correlations among auxiliary/total revenue, enrollment/faculty, tuition 
19:486:41855:28:28:71:533:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:plus state appropriations per student, and endowment per student.  The enrollment/faculty ratio, 
19:487:41952:28:27:71:504:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:or the student-teacher ratio, is positively correlated with auxiliary/total revenue.  Since an 
19:488:42047:27:28:71:522:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increase in the student-teacher ratio spreads limited resources over more students, it also may 
19:489:42143:28:27:71:517:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:indicate financial duress41.  Tuition plus state appropriations per student and endowment per 
19:490:42237:27:28:72:531:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:student capture more abundant resources per student.  They are the opposite of financial duress 
19:491:42333:28:27:72:514:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Ehrenberg, 2002).  They should be, and are, negatively correlated with the financial duress 
19:492:42426:27:32:72:469:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:Times:B:indicators, which in this study are auxiliary/total revenue and enrollment/faculty.   
19:493:42511:32:24:108:368:263:257:Times:144:g_d0_f3:C:V. Growth of University Research    
19:494:42546:24:27:90:520:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:I now use the university panel data described in Section IV to provide an overview of the 
19:495:42636:27:28:72:537:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:growth of university research.  Understanding these facts is helpful in interpreting the regression 
19:496:42736:28:27:72:512:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:analysis of university research in Section VI.  To this end, I have composed three summary 
19:497:42827:27:28:72:531:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tables that are designed to facilitate discussion of trends in university research productivity and 
19:498:42927:28:20:72:353:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the U.S. slowdown in publication rates during the 1990s.   
19:499:42986:20:8:108:254:109:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
19:500:43046:8:11:72:305:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:40 Hospital revenues are separate from auxiliary revenues. 
19:501:43105:11:16:72:534:90:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:41  An alternative view is that a higher student-teacher ratio automatically increases the share of auxiliary fees.  It is 
19:502:43228:16:0:72:294:74:100:g_d0_f3:42:g_d0_f3:F:by no means perfect as an indicator of financial duress. 
20:503:43289:0:27:90:534:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 5 presents totals of papers, citation-weighted papers, PhD degrees awarded, and R&D 
20:504:43379:27:28:72:519:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:stock in private and public universities.  The data consist of 620 university-fields (out of 648 
20:505:43476:28:27:72:503:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:possible), observed over 1982-1999, for which there are no missing values.  To aid in the 
20:506:43566:27:28:72:541:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:interpretation, I report values relative to 1982 in square brackets.  In brief, the data tell us that the 
20:507:43672:28:28:72:501:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:output of papers grows by slightly more (slightly less) than 50 percent in private (public) 
20:508:43764:28:27:71:535:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities; that citations grow by 125 percent in both groups (from 1982-1995); and that PhDs 
20:509:43860:27:28:72:507:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:grow by a third in both.  Since citations rise with the growing ease of citation and with the 
20:510:43954:28:27:72:506:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:number of researchers who cite, citation growth is best regarded as an upper bound on the 
20:511:44044:27:28:71:535:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:growth of research output.  But since papers have genuinely become more influential, growth of 
20:512:44139:28:28:71:537:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:papers is a lower bound.  Therefore, growth of research output lies between 50 and 125 percent.  
20:513:44236:28:27:89:521:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:This provides a broad range of growth in research output, but what about input? I start by 
20:514:44327:27:28:71:539:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:examining the behavior of R&D stock deflated by the implicit GDP deflator.  This grows by 105 
20:515:44421:28:27:71:521:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent (130 percent) in private (public) schools.  R&D growth exceeds publication and PhD 
20:516:44512:27:28:71:539:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:growth: surely, one supposes, this is a recipe for a slowdown in research productivity.  But R&D 
20:517:44609:28:27:71:518:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:growth is overstated, because the GDP deflator understates cost increases in universities and 
20:518:44703:27:28:71:538:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:overstates growth of real R&D.  The evidence in Table 13 below, on rising real compensation of 
20:519:44798:28:28:71:230:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:faculty, helps to make this clear. 
20:520:44833:28:27:89:527:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:For this reason I prefer the Bureau of Economic Analysis (BEA) price index for university 
20:521:44923:27:28:71:541:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:R&D (Robbins and Moylan, 2007), because it takes university wage costs into account, and I use 
20:522:45018:28:27:71:537:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the BEA index to deflate R&D stock in all the regressions to follow.  When I use the BEA index 
20:523:45113:27:28:71:485:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:instead of the implicit GDP deflator to calculate real R&D, I find that R&D in private 
20:524:45200:28:28:71:532:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities grows by 72 percent, not 105 percent. Likewise I find that growth in public schools 
20:525:45297:28:0:71:535:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is 93 percent, not 130 percent.  Using the improved deflator real R&D grows by 70 (90) percent 
21:526:45397:0:27:72:524:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in private (public) universities, while research output grows by 50/125 percent in both. In this 
21:527:45494:27:28:71:428:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:way the gap narrows between growth of articles and growth of real R&D. 
21:528:45565:28:27:90:532:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Even so, growth of real R&D is likely to be overstated despite the use of the BEA deflator.  
21:529:45658:27:28:72:511:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:First, inter-university grants probably grow in importance during this time because of large 
21:530:45751:28:28:72:511:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:projects in biology and other fields.  Since grants are not apportioned among schools in the 
21:531:45844:28:27:72:523:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:statistics until well after 1999, R&D is increasingly over-counted because of this.  Second, an 
21:532:45940:27:28:72:514:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increasing amount of funding could be targeted for training of graduate students rather than 
21:533:46033:28:27:72:506:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:faculty research. To assess research productivity with more accuracy it would be useful to 
21:534:46124:27:28:72:534:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:separate funds for research from funds for pure training.  A related point might be important, if  
21:535:46223:28:28:72:536:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities move from institutional to grant support of graduate students.  To that extent, grants 
21:536:46323:28:27:72:530:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:replace internal funds and they are not additional funds for research.  I mention these problems 
21:537:46420:27:28:72:541:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:not because I have solutions to them but in the interest of producing better statistics on university 
21:538:46522:28:27:72:172:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:R&D in the future.   
21:539:46543:27:28:90:529:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 5 shows that publications in private universities grow more slowly than R&D stock.  
21:540:46633:28:27:72:534:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:The same point applies even more strongly to public universities. While growth of papers slows 
21:541:46728:27:28:72:538:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:down during 1995-1999 in private universities, it virtually stops in public universities. However, 
21:542:46827:28:28:72:535:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the growth rate of papers recovers somewhat during 2000-2005 (see Figure 5) so this slowdown 
21:543:46920:28:27:72:219:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is to some extent temporary42. 
21:544:46951:27:28:90:542:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 6 constructs ratios of papers, citations, and PhD students to R&D stocks using the GDP 
21:545:47044:28:27:72:532:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and BEA deflators, and it examines their growth.  Using the BEA deflator, papers per million $ 
21:546:47139:27:28:72:513:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:decline over time in private schools by -11% but the decline is -23% in public universities.  
21:547:47233:28:20:72:540:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Citations per million also grow significantly faster in private universities.  In comparing research 
21:548:47334:20:8:108:254:109:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
21:549:47394:8:16:72:534:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:42 For all academic institutions, total scientific papers published fell from 139,168 in 1995 to 138,472 in 1999.  But 
21:550:47513:16:11:72:520:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:by 2005 this total had increased to 159,972.  Numbers of scientific papers reflect year of entry into the database 
21:551:47628:11:0:72:477:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:rather than year of publication.  See National Science Board, 2008, Chapter 5, Appendix Table 5-36. 
22:552:47733:0:27:72:514:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:productivity, it is useful to remember that faculty compensation rises by almost one percent 
22:553:47826:27:28:72:493:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:faster a year in private universities.  Almost paradoxically this may explain why papers 
22:554:47915:28:27:72:540:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(citations) per million $ of R&D fall less (rise more).  It is because labor quality grows at a faster 
22:555:48018:27:28:72:538:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rate in private universities due to faster wage growth in these universities.  Finally, PhD students 
22:556:48119:28:28:72:375:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:per million $ decline by 50 percent in both types of university. 
22:557:48184:28:27:90:537:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 7 takes a different look at university resources.  It records enrollment, tenure track and 
22:558:48281:27:28:72:518:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:non-tenure track faculty, tuition (in public universities, tuition plus state appropriations). All 
22:559:48380:28:27:72:540:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:variables are at the university level.  Values relative to 1982 are again placed in square brackets.  
22:560:48482:27:28:72:500:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:These measures track teaching loads as well as human and financial resources over time. 
22:561:48570:28:28:90:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Growth in enrollments in both private and public institutions is about 10 percent by 1997.  
22:562:48662:28:27:72:508:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Since PhD degrees increase by one third, enrollment shifts towards (more costly) graduate 
22:563:48752:27:28:72:540:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:education.  Numbers of faculty grow by 25 percent in private universities, but by eight percent in 
22:564:48851:28:27:72:535:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:public universities.  Most of the growth in private universities occurs at the end, during a period 
22:565:48951:27:28:72:545:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of rapid growth in stock market and endowment values.  Its effects will be felt in the 21st century.  
22:566:49053:28:27:71:537:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Tuition revenue grows by 124 percent in private universities but tuition plus state appropriations 
22:567:49152:27:28:71:522:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in public universities grow by just 46 percent.  The divergence in resources becomes obvious 
22:568:49245:28:28:71:533:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:during the 1990s.  It helps to account for differences in private-public productivity, since I shall 
22:569:49346:28:27:71:294:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:show that current revenues support research.   
22:570:49393:27:28:89:527:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: Endowments grow at the same rate in all institutions, though the difference in endowment 
22:571:49483:28:27:71:527:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:per faculty remains large. It is 1.39 million in private universities versus 0.15 million in public 
22:572:49583:27:28:71:495:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities. Endowment is simply too small in most public institutions to affect faculty 
22:573:49673:28:0:71:176:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:resources very much. 
23:574:49699:0:27:90:514:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Together Tables 5 and 7 provide a new perspective on university research productivity.  
23:575:49787:27:28:72:518:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Table 5 shows that papers increase by 50 percent during this period, while citation-weighted 
23:576:49880:28:27:72:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:papers increase by 125 percent.  Table 7 shows that faculty increase by 10-25 percent.  Papers 
23:577:49975:27:28:72:521:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:per faculty increase by either measure, and this draws attention to the point made earlier, that 
23:578:50072:28:28:72:508:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:growth of university R&D is overstated.  At the same time, research productivity in public 
23:579:50163:28:31:72:346:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities has clearly fallen behind that of the privates. 
23:580:50224:31:28:108:285:539:257:Times:144:g_d0_f3:C:VI. Regression Findings 
23:581:50246:28:23:126:259:511:257:Times:144:g_d0_f3:C:A. Equation Setup   
23:582:50265:23:28:90:539:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:To better understand the determinants of research productivity, I turn to a regression analysis 
23:583:50360:28:28:71:540:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of the university, field and year panel. Tables 8 and 9 present pooled OLS regressions for private 
23:584:50459:28:27:71:541:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and public universities.  By pooled, I specifically mean regressions that combine fields in a given 
23:585:50559:27:28:72:520:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:university.  As I have shown, the university-field dimension of the data allows for variability 
23:586:50655:28:28:72:474:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:within universities that helps to identify effects of R&D stock and other variables.   
23:587:50742:28:33:107:537:349:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The regressions follow three basic formats that I describe next.  Let ijty be the logarithm 
23:588:50834:33:32:71:499:316:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of research output (papers or citations) in fieldi, universityj, at timet, let ijtx consist of 
23:589:50929:32:28:72:539:284:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:logarithms of R&D stock, graduate students, and current revenue defined by (1), (3) and (2); and 
23:590:51026:28:33:72:481:256:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:let jtz stand for financial variables at the university level (endowment in logarithms; 
23:591:51114:33:31:72:528:223:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:auxiliary/total revenue, and enrollment/faculty).  Also,iD is a vector of field dummies.43 Then 
23:592:51210:31:28:71:332:192:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the “total” equation that omits university dummies is: 
23:593:51265:28:26:71:291:164:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(4)  ijtjiiijtxijtueDxty++′+′++=δββα 0 
23:594:51302:26:18:71:453:138:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Financial variablesjtzare omitted from (4), but they are included in (4') below: 
23:595:51383:18:7:108:254:120:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
23:596:51443:7:16:72:515:113:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:43 In other regressions I include shares of full and associate professors to capture aging effects.  The shares are 
23:597:51559:16:12:72:540:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:insignificant. Unlike individual productivity of scientists (Stephan and Levin, 1991, 1992) where age is significantly 
23:598:51678:12:11:72:528:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:negative, at the university and field level rank is insignificant.  One explanation for the difference is that selective 
23:599:51799:11:0:72:485:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:pressures favor more productive researchers. Promotion in the aggregate counteracts individual aging.  
24:600:51907:0:26:72:326:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(4')    ijtjiijtzijtxijtueDzxty++′+′+′++=δγββα 0 
24:601:51954:26:33:72:511:682:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:In (4) and (4′) jeis a university error component that may be correlated with the right hand 
24:602:52047:33:32:72:527:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:variables whileijtu is a transitory component that is uncorrelated over time both with itself and 
24:603:52145:32:27:72:303:617:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with the contemporaneous right hand variables. 
24:604:52192:27:29:108:375:590:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The “within” equation adds university dummies to (4'): 
24:605:52247:29:26:71:339:561:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(5)  ijtjjiijtzijtxijtuDDzxty+′+′+′+′++=δδγββα 0 
24:606:52294:26:35:71:508:535:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:In (5), the vector of university dummiesjD absorbs the university error component, so that
24:607:52384:35:0:117:93:500:48:Times:142:g_d0_f7:?:jjjDe δ′=
24:608:52392:0:37:122:136:508:64:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:?:44. 
24:609:52396:37:28:90:525:471:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:I also include time trend in (4), (4′), and (5) to indicate residual growth.  If trend increases 
24:610:52493:28:27:71:528:443:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:when university effects are included, then this may indicate that research output shifts towards 
24:611:52590:27:32:71:444:416:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities where output grows more slowly (Adams and Clemmons, 2009). 
24:612:52662:32:24:126:425:384:257:Times:144:g_d0_f3:C:B. Pooled Regressions: Private Universities  
24:613:52706:24:27:90:539:360:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 8 reports estimates for private universities.  Following (4), equation 8.1 includes trend, 
24:614:52803:27:28:71:510:333:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:R&D stock and the stock of graduate students. All are highly significant, and together they 
24:615:52895:28:27:71:510:305:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:explain most of the variation in papers45.  The elasticity of R&D stock is 0.41 while that of 
24:616:52989:27:28:72:513:278:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:graduate students is 0.16.  It follows that an expansion of R&D and graduate students of 10 
24:617:53081:28:28:72:532:250:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent results in 5.7 percent more papers in private universities, indicating diminishing returns 
24:618:53180:28:27:71:537:222:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to research resources.  Following (4′) 8.2 adds financial variables.  Lagged tuition is linked to an 
24:619:53281:27:28:71:508:195:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increase in papers, but this is not statistically significant.  The coefficient of endowment is 
24:620:53377:28:27:71:523:167:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:positive and marginally significant.  Auxiliary/total revenue and enrollment/faculty (financial 
24:621:53473:27:31:71:535:140:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:duress) reduce research output, but again are not statistically significant.  As in (5), equation 8.3 
24:622:53575:31:8:108:254:109:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
24:623:53635:8:16:72:515:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:44 See Hsiao (2003, Chapters 2 and 3) for derivations of estimators of the slope coefficients in total and within 
24:624:53749:16:7:72:122:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:regressions. 
24:625:53762:7:0:72:302:78:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:45 See Adams and Griliches (1998) for a related analysis. 
25:626:53825:0:27:72:507:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:adds university dummies.  Tuition revenue now enters significantly as do the indicators of 
25:627:53916:27:28:72:536:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:financial duress.  In 8.2 and 8.3, trend becomes insignificant so that growth of research output is 
25:628:54016:28:27:72:508:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:fully explained. R&D stock and graduate students decline slightly, but remain significant.  
25:629:54108:27:28:90:522:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Equations 8.4-8.6 explain five-year citations received.  While the elasticity of R&D stock 
25:630:54199:28:28:72:527:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increases compared to the earlier regressions for papers, that of graduate students declines and 
25:631:54296:28:27:72:530:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:becomes insignificant.  Endowment is linked to an increase in citations, suggesting that private 
25:632:54393:27:28:72:541:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities use endowment to buy release time and hire star faculty.  As with papers, trend is not 
25:633:54493:28:27:72:328:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:significant once the financial indicators are included. 
25:634:54549:27:28:90:504:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:In all these production functions and those in succeeding tables, the sum of the output 
25:635:54637:28:28:72:546:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:elasticities across R&D stock, graduate students, tuition revenue, and endowment is less than 1.0.  
25:636:54737:28:27:72:515:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:This suggests decreasing returns to scale in university research and limits to university size, 
25:637:54833:27:28:72:529:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consistent with Adams and Clemmons (2009).  The relevance of this point is that, allowing for 
25:638:54927:28:27:72:529:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:fixed costs of research and after the efficient scale is reached, research may be better shifted to 
25:639:55027:27:28:72:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities in which it was previously missing. I shall return to this point in the summary and 
25:640:55124:28:31:72:213:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:conclusion in Section VII.     
25:641:55155:31:24:126:417:291:257:Times:257:Times:C:C. Pooled Regressions: Public Universities 
25:642:55197:24:28:90:526:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 9 reports results for public universities.  In general, output elasticities of R&D stock 
25:643:55292:28:27:72:537:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:are less than in Table 8 for private schools.  One difference, though, is the larger elasticity of the 
25:644:55395:27:28:72:530:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:stock of graduate students, about 0.1 higher and significant throughout.  This may indicate that 
25:645:55492:28:27:72:526:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:graduate student assistants are funded in public universities, to a larger extent, by means other 
25:646:55590:27:28:72:520:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:than R&D, such as teaching assistantships.  Research output rises, usually significantly, with 
25:647:55685:28:28:72:523:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tuition plus state appropriations.  Endowment does not contribute to research output in public 
25:648:55780:28:0:72:505:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities, because amounts per faculty member are too small to matter.  Auxiliary/total 
26:649:55876:0:27:72:517:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:revenues and enrollment/faculty enter with the expected negative signs, but are insignificant 
26:650:55970:27:28:72:300:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:once university effects are taken into account.   
26:651:56020:28:27:90:529:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The trend coefficient is also greater in the public university regressions.  The coefficient of 
26:652:56116:27:28:72:511:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:trend is even higher in the “within” regressions (9.3 and 9.6) than in total.  Again, this may 
26:653:56211:28:28:72:542:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:reflect a shift of research towards schools where output growth is slower (Adams and Clemmons, 
26:654:56306:28:27:72:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:2009).  Some of trend growth could also be due to knowledge flows from private universities, 
26:655:56399:27:28:72:523:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:since knowledge flows are more likely to take place from higher to lower ranked departments 
26:656:56491:28:27:72:514:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Adams, Clemmons, and Stephan, 2006) and since top departments are more often found in 
26:657:56578:27:32:72:176:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:private universities.   
26:658:56602:32:24:126:492:456:257:Times:257:Times:C:D. Regressions Stratified by Rank of University-Field 
26:659:56655:24:27:90:528:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Let us now consider university-fields stratified into groups according to top 20, middle 40, 
26:660:56748:27:28:71:538:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and bottom 40 percent rankings.  Table 10 contains frequency distributions of the top 20, middle 
26:661:56845:28:27:71:528:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:40, and bottom 40 by private and public ownership. The top 20 and middle 40 percent account 
26:662:56937:27:28:71:536:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:for most of the private school observations.  In contrast public school observations cluster in the 
26:663:57037:28:27:71:516:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:middle and bottom 40 percent. Even so, public universities contain almost half of the top 20 
26:664:57130:27:28:71:489:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent university-fields. The stratified regressions take this into account by analyzing 
26:665:57220:28:28:71:289:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:differences in quality wherever they occur.    
26:666:57267:28:27:89:518:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 11 reports estimates of (4′) and (5).  It shows results for the top 20, middle 40, and 
26:667:57360:27:28:71:531:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:bottom 40 percent in Panels A, B, and C respectively.  Because I separate university-fields into 
26:668:57457:28:40:71:534:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:groups by rank, the regressions are stratified, though they are pooled across fields46.   I focus on 
26:669:57558:40:8:108:254:144:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
26:670:57618:8:16:72:505:136:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:46 Following Section IV, top 20 percent regressions include the top five in astronomy, the top 15 in biology, 
26:671:57728:16:12:72:530:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:medicine, and engineering, and the top 10 in all other fields.  Middle 40 percent regressions include the next 10 in 
26:672:57845:12:11:72:537:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:astronomy, the next 30 in biology, medicine, and engineering, and the next 20 in all other fields. Bottom 40 percent 
26:673:57962:11:12:72:513:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:regressions include the bottom 10 in astronomy, the bottom 30 in biology, medicine, and engineering, and the 
26:674:58071:12:11:72:191:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:bottom 20 in all other fields.  
26:675:58103:11:0:72:75:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F: 
27:676:58108:0:27:72:510:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:key variables consisting of trend, R&D, and graduate students, not reporting results for the 
27:677:58201:27:28:72:391:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:financial variables, although these are included in the regressions. 
27:678:58270:28:27:108:522:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: Top 20 percent university-fields obtain more research output from R&D and graduate 
27:679:58353:27:28:72:516:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:students than the middle or bottom 40 percent47.  Indeed, graduate students in the bottom 40 
27:680:58446:28:28:72:516:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent fail to make any significant contribution to research.  This implies that their primary 
27:681:58542:28:27:72:539:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:duties are to teach and work on thesis research.  This and the faculty time needed for dissertation 
27:682:58642:27:28:72:495:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:work, reduce the net student contribution to zero in bottom 40 percent university-fields. 
27:683:58732:28:27:108:509:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: Below the top 20 percent the pattern in the trend coefficients suggests that research 
27:684:58818:27:28:72:539:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:output grows more rapidly in the within regressions, which include university effects, than in the 
27:685:58917:28:28:72:511:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:total regressions that exclude these effects. As before, this pattern could be due to a shift in 
27:686:59014:28:31:72:472:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:output towards universities in which growth is less (Adams and Clemmons, 2009). 
27:687:59094:31:24:126:451:401:257:Times:257:Times:C:E.  Faculty Compensation and Wage Structure  
27:688:59136:24:27:90:499:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The empirical work concludes with a regression analysis of faculty compensation by 
27:689:59219:27:28:72:537:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:professorial rank—or in other words, the academic wage structure. Studying this structure could 
27:690:59315:28:27:72:528:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:help us to further understand the financial condition of universities.  The dependent variable is 
27:691:59413:27:28:71:527:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the logarithm of wages plus fringe benefits in ’92 $ at the full and assistant professor ranks48.   
27:692:59513:28:28:71:528:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:These are university-wide averages, since HEGIS, which is their source, does not collect wage 
27:693:59607:28:27:71:511:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:data by university-field. Since compensation is an average I cannot estimate a typical wage 
27:694:59699:27:28:71:537:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:equation where wages are a function of education, experience, and tenure.  But faculty quality is 
27:695:59797:28:29:71:535:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:reflected in the logarithm of the university-wide R&D stock per faculty, the logarithm of tuition 
27:696:59895:29:8:108:254:155:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
27:697:59955:8:16:72:525:147:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:47 These results are similar to findings for Top 10 universities not reported here.  The Top 10 are selected on the 
27:698:60070:16:11:72:518:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:basis of top 10 citation impact per paper in a set of 21 fields during 1981-1993.  Schools ranked as top 10 most 
27:699:60183:11:12:72:522:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:frequently among these fields are considered a Top 10 University.  They include eight private schools (Harvard, 
27:700:60295:12:11:72:521:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Yale, Chicago, MIT, Stanford, Princeton, Cornell, and California Institute of Technology) as well as two public 
27:701:60407:11:12:72:530:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:schools (Berkeley and the University of Washington). It should come as no surprise that top 20 percent university-
27:702:60521:12:7:72:251:85:100:g_d0_f3:576:Times:C:fields predominate in Top 10 universities.  
27:703:60565:7:0:72:485:78:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:48 All monetary variables beside R&D are deflated by the GDP implicit price deflator indexed to 1992. 
28:704:60672:0:27:72:510:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:revenue per faculty (private schools) or tuition plus state appropriations per faculty (public 
28:705:60767:27:28:72:484:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:schools), the logarithm of endowment per faculty, and the financial duress indicators, 
28:706:60854:28:27:72:531:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:auxiliary/total revenue and enrollment/faculty.  In constructing per capita variables on the right 
28:707:60953:27:28:72:537:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:hand side of the wage equations, I lag the number of faculty to limit division error bias.  Besides 
28:708:61053:28:28:72:509:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the above I include trend to capture general wage growth, and a cost of living indicator for 
28:709:61146:28:27:72:542:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:whether a university is located in a large city (in the U.S., a Consolidated Metropolitan Statistical 
28:710:61248:27:29:72:209:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Area).  The specification is: 
28:711:61278:29:25:72:359:514:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(6)  jtLjtut+′+++=jt0x City  Large )Wage(Logβββα 
28:712:61323:25:27:72:499:489:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:These are “total” wage regressions that omit university effects because wage variation is 
28:713:61413:27:28:72:465:462:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:insufficient in the within-university dimension to permit a “within” specification. 
28:714:61497:28:27:107:541:434:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Table 12 contains the results.  The dependent variable in 12.1 and 12.4 is the logarithm of 
28:715:61589:27:28:71:485:407:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:full professor compensation; in 12.2 and 12.5 it is the logarithm of assistant professor 
28:716:61678:28:28:71:396:379:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compensation; and in 12.3 and 12.6 it is the difference of the two.   
28:717:61748:28:27:107:535:351:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: Starting with the results for full and assistant professors, the trend coefficients show that 
28:718:61842:27:28:71:492:324:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:real compensation grows at about 1.5 percent a year, all else equal, but faster in private 
28:719:61933:28:27:71:536:296:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities, especially at the assistant professor level, where it grows at 2.5 percent49.  Location 
28:720:62035:27:28:71:528:269:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in a large city raises private school wages by 5-10 percent, although it has no significant effect 
28:721:62134:28:27:71:530:241:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:on wages in public schools, probably because state institutions are mostly located outside large 
28:722:62231:27:28:71:486:214:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cities.  For full professors in private universities, R&D stock and endowment increase 
28:723:62318:28:28:71:505:186:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compensation.  Besides trend, the only significant determinant of compensation in public  
28:724:62408:28:37:71:442:158:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities is current revenue consisting of tuition plus state appropriations. 
28:725:62489:37:7:108:254:121:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f4:?:                                                            
28:726:62549:7:17:72:501:114:42:g_d0_f5:100:g_d0_f3:F:49 The compensation gap between private and public universities rises at the rate of 0.8% a year.  In simple 
28:727:62658:17:12:71:539:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:regressions that include trend and intercept, I find that, relative to the GDP deflator, both full and assistant professor 
28:728:62781:12:11:71:519:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:compensation grows at 2.3% per year in private universities and at 1.5% per year in public universities. Top 10 
28:729:62893:11:0:71:455:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:university compensation grows at 2.2% per year. R2s for these regressions range from 0.3-0.5.   
29:730:62994:0:27:108:542:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C: Equations 12.3 and 12.6 display the results for the difference in compensation for full and 
29:731:63086:27:28:72:540:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:assistant professors.  In the private university equation (12.3), we see that location in a large city, 
29:732:63190:28:27:71:477:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tuition, and endowment increase the wage premium for senior faculty, but trend and 
29:733:63273:27:28:71:538:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:enrollment/faculty decrease it.  In the public university equation (12.6), the wage structure is flat 
29:734:63375:28:28:72:515:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:across ranks.  Together the findings suggest that successful researchers have an incentive to 
29:735:63469:28:31:71:579:570:144:g_d0_f3:257:Times:B:move to private universities that increases with the rank of full professor.                                        
29:736:63585:31:24:107:413:539:257:Times:144:g_d0_f3:C:VII.  Discussion, Synthesis, and Conclusion  
29:737:63628:24:27:89:537:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Is the U.S. losing its preeminence in higher education?  The evidence presented in this paper 
29:738:63722:27:28:71:541:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:suggests that in a relative sense it is.  Sections II and III tell a story of rapid postwar expansion of 
29:739:63827:28:28:71:518:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:U.S. universities, followed by a tapering off after 1980. A series of natural experiments took 
29:740:63922:28:27:71:535:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:place in the 1930s and 1940s that contributed to this growth.  Because of their exogeneity, these 
29:741:64020:27:28:71:510:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:early events may in time capture the imagination of researchers studying higher education. 
29:742:64111:28:27:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:In the early years growth of U.S. universities was aided by refugee scientists, with foreign 
29:743:64204:27:28:71:524:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:graduate students playing a larger role after 1980.  Additional early factors that contributed to 
29:744:64302:28:27:71:532:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:expansion of U.S. universities include a broadening of access to universities, increased military 
29:745:64400:27:28:71:541:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:research during World War II and the Cold War, and the expansion of high technology industries 
29:746:64495:28:28:71:537:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:during the postwar period.  Since the 1980s we observe more rapid growth of academic research 
29:747:64589:28:27:71:532:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in Europe, and especially East Asia, that implies convergence in world science and engineering 
29:748:64684:27:28:71:223:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and a decline in the U.S. share. 
29:749:64717:28:27:89:505:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:But this is not the entire story. Most recently, in the 1990s, we observe a slowdown of 
29:750:64805:27:28:72:533:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:publication output in the U.S. This becomes the central puzzle of the paper, and Sections IV-VI 
29:751:64901:28:28:72:529:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:address it using panel data on universities, fields and years.  In Section IV I describe the panel, 
29:752:65001:28:0:71:524:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and in Section V I present growth facts concerning U.S. university research. These reveal that 
30:753:65101:0:27:72:534:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:much of the slowdown in publication is located in public universities.  While R&D stocks grow 
30:754:65195:27:28:72:530:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:more rapidly in public than private schools, current revenues grow more slowly.  This suggests 
30:755:65290:28:27:72:498:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that public universities fall behind because of slower growth in their financial resources. 
30:756:65382:27:28:90:506:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:The regression findings in Section VI indicate a fairly similar if not perfectly identical 
30:757:65473:28:28:72:534:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:production process in public and private universities.  On average, both obtain similar increases 
30:758:65571:28:27:72:542:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in scientific papers from similar combined increases in R&D, graduate students, tuition revenues, 
30:759:65669:27:28:72:492:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and endowment.  This is true even though graduate students play a larger role in public 
30:760:65757:28:27:72:535:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities, perhaps because research is cross-subsidized by teaching assistantships more of the 
30:761:65855:27:28:72:542:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:time.  In view of this broad similarity,  a divergence in research output over time, in which public 
30:762:65956:28:28:72:541:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities fall behind, can only be accounted for by a lower rate of increase in public university 
30:763:66057:28:27:72:230:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:resources, as Section V reveals.  
30:764:66091:27:28:90:533:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:In support of this hypothesis compensation in private universities rises almost one percent a 
30:765:66185:28:27:71:522:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:year faster than in public universities.  And besides, wages are flat across professorial rank in 
30:766:66283:27:28:71:506:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:public universities, whereas they rise noticeably with rank in private universities.  All this 
30:767:66378:28:27:71:526:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:suggests reasons for top scientists to migrate from public to private universities.  Therefore, in 
30:768:66477:27:28:71:538:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:several ways slower growth in current revenues in public universities produces slower growth of 
30:769:66573:28:28:71:157:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:research as well.  
30:770:66592:28:27:89:537:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:At the same time, (mostly federal) research funding expands at a faster rate in public schools 
30:771:66687:27:28:72:541:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Adams and Clemmons, 2009).  Together this tells an interesting story of state and federal policy 
30:772:66785:28:27:72:538:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:interactions.  Even as (mostly federal) R&D is expanding, the states are subjected to a portion of 
30:773:66884:27:28:71:531:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rising health care costs under Medicaid. In addition, some are subject to mandated equalization 
30:774:66980:28:28:71:515:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of K-12 education expenditures which raise the cost of elementary and secondary education 
30:775:67070:28:0:71:499:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Murray, Evans, and Schwab, 1998).  Towards the end of the period some states commit 
31:776:67160:0:27:72:523:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:themselves to pre-paid tuition plans that are inadequately funded (Rizzo, 2006). So growth of 
31:777:67254:27:28:71:524:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:mostly federal research dollars is cancelled out by the slower growth of state dollars in public 
31:778:67351:28:27:71:132:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities. 
31:779:67365:27:28:89:534:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:An obvious question that arises is whether this situation will persist.  If it is temporary, then 
31:780:67463:28:28:71:494:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the downward fluctuations of finances of public universities during the 1990s would be 
31:781:67550:28:27:71:510:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compensated by upward fluctuations at a later time, leaving public institutions on the same 
31:782:67642:27:28:71:509:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:unaltered trend line with little to be concerned about in the long run.  But if the situation is 
31:783:67739:28:27:71:526:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:permanent and state funding remains below trend and perhaps increasingly so, then top public 
31:784:67832:27:28:71:535:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities would have to seek alternative sources of funding to begin to catch up to top private 
31:785:67931:28:28:71:510:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities.  They might for example, seek to obtain freely floating tuition from parents of 
31:786:68025:28:27:71:514:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:students anywhere in the world.  But this solution seems unlikely given the charters of state 
31:787:68119:27:28:71:534:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities and ownership of their real assets by the states.  More likely is a gradual removal of 
31:788:68219:28:27:71:527:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tuition price controls to in-state families amidst a frank recognition that price caps deny public 
31:789:68318:27:28:71:529:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities the resources that are essential to a good education.  Still another solution revolves 
31:790:68418:28:27:71:502:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:around increased commercialization of university inventions as well as increased sales of 
31:791:68508:27:28:71:502:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:merchandise and entertainment, though the latter are hardly consistent with the academic 
31:792:68597:28:28:71:533:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:missions of these institutions.  All these adjustments to the new realities seem destined to occur 
31:793:68696:28:27:71:519:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:slowly, so that relative shortfalls of public universities are likely to persist for years to come. 
31:794:68796:27:28:89:525:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:On a world-wide scale, the relatively faster growth of universities in newly industrializing 
31:795:68889:28:27:71:511:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:countries will continue.  This is because this growth is part of a convergence process in the 
31:796:68983:27:28:71:511:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:developing world, in which steady state incomes and growth rates increase as a function of 
31:797:69074:28:0:71:504:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increases in education and stocks of knowledge.  Even if funding problems of U.S. public 
32:798:69168:0:27:72:533:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:universities could be resolved through improved mechanisms of finance, the decline in the U.S. 
32:799:69263:27:28:72:317:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:share of world science will likely persist.                
32:800:69322:28:27:90:539:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:Yet another possibility arises. All that we have seen in this paper, which covers more than 80 
32:801:69417:27:28:72:542:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent of academic research in the U.S., consists of a fixed set of top 110 institutions.   Tables 8, 
32:802:69520:28:28:72:534:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:9 and 11 show that these universities are subject to decreasing returns to scale in research, since 
32:803:69620:28:27:72:542:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the sum of the output elasticities of R&D stock, graduate students,  and financial resources is less 
32:804:69721:27:28:72:524:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:than one. Since this is the definition of decreasing returns, one might suppose that beyond the 
32:805:69817:28:27:72:522:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:efficient scale, more growth could be obtained at less cost by spreading research funds over a 
32:806:69912:27:28:72:529:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:wider range of universities. Of course, organizational assets in smaller research institutions are 
32:807:70011:28:28:72:510:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:not necessarily the equal of those in top 110 schools.  It follows that if sustained growth of 
32:808:70106:28:27:72:536:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:research output is the objective, then the challenge is not only that of spreading resources across 
32:809:70206:27:28:72:507:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:more schools, but also that of replicating the assets of top universities.  At present, growth 
32:810:70301:28:27:72:592:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:appears to be more rapid in universities where this kind of replication remains an open question.
